# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Connect REST API v1 to v2 Migration

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Kafka Connect REST API: the v1 connector resource handlers, the v2 connector resource handlers, and the version routing logic. Identify what changed between v1 and v2 in the task status and error response schemas.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

76-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka Connect REST API implementation in the Apache Kafka repository. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

### REST API Resource Handlers
The Kafka Connect REST API is implemented through several resource classes:
- **ConnectorsResource** - Main handler for connector management endpoints (`/connectors`)
- **RootResource** - Server info and health check endpoints
- **InternalConnectResource** - Inter-worker communication
- **ConnectorPluginsResource** - Plugin discovery and validation
- **LoggingResource** - Dynamic logging management

### Task Status Schema (ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState)
Located in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/ConnectorStateInfo.java`, the task status includes:
- `id` (int) - Task ID
- `state` (String) - Current state (running, paused, failed, restarting)
- `worker_id` (String) - Worker identifier
- `trace` (String) - Error message when applicable
- `version` (String) - Plugin version information

### Error Response Schema (ErrorMessage)
Located in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/ErrorMessage.java`, with fields:
- `error_code` (int) - HTTP status or error code
- `message` (String) - Error description

### Version Routing
The implementation uses a single unified REST API interface without explicit v1/v2 routes. Instead:
- **RestServer** (abstract base) manages the Jetty server
- **ConnectRestServer** (concrete implementation) registers all resources
- Request forwarding between workers is handled by **HerderRequestHandler**
- Error mapping by **ConnectExceptionMapper** converts exceptions to standardized ErrorMessage responses

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all r

        <li> For Stream-Stream joins, all three types (inner, outer, left) handle out-of-order records correctly.</li>\\n336:         <li> For Stream-Table joins, if not using versioned stores, then This is done through API versioning.\n118: \n119: <p>Before each request is sent, the client sends the API key and the API version.
